Local News

Formal Announcement of the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Association

Measures for Handling Japanese Goods

All Orders and Inventory Strictly Prohibited from Movement

Overseas Compatriots Issue Reports on Their Tragic Suffering

The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee, having held its first committee meeting the day before yesterday and elected Yu Qiaqing as chairman of the committee, and having resolved on various measures, officially convened its first standing committee meeting yesterday and formally announced measures for handling Japanese goods. The various departments have also begun operations. The details are as follows:

Standing Committee Meeting: Yesterday at 2 PM, the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee held its first committee meeting. Wang Xiaolai, Tao Baichuan, Hou Dachun, Wang Yansong, Lu Jingshi, and Chen Tingrui were present. Chairman Yu Qiaqing was unable to attend due to personally convening the preparatory meeting for Siming University, and Wang Xiaolai was publicly elected as temporary chairman. Yan E’sheng served as secretary, and the following resolutions were passed: (1) Committee Member Wang Yansong was appointed to the Economic Committee. (2) Committee Member Xu Jiqing was designated as convener of the Economic Committee. (3) The number of members on the Design Committee was set between nine and twenty-seven, including (A) economic experts, (B) those with experience in certain industries, (C) customs brokers, and (D) transportation operators. Li Quanshi, Xu Yongzuo, Zhu Yinong, Guo Waifeng, Pan Xulun, Chen Songyuan, Zhu Wenqi, Wu Zhihao, Zhou Jingzhai, Gui Yanfang, and Chen Haiqiu were nominated as committee members, and Chen Songyuan was designated as convener. The organizational regulations were entrusted to the secretary for drafting. (4) Zheng Chengqing was nominated as deputy director of the General Affairs Department, Xi Yushu as deputy director of the Registration Department, Chen Yafu as deputy director of the Propaganda Department, and Zhang Yichen as deputy director of the Storage Department. Confirmation will be requested at the next full committee meeting. (5) The standards for hiring staff were resolved: (A) Staff must be introduced and guaranteed by two or more members of this committee (a separate form of guarantee will be specified). (B) Each department will have divisions, and each division will have one chief secretary, several secretaries, and assistant secretaries. (C) Staff for each department will be nominated by the department director, approved by the standing committee, and reported to the full committee. (6) Staff badges and certificates will be produced promptly. Detailed methods for boycotting Japanese goods were also discussed, and the meeting adjourned at 5 PM.

Establishment Announcement: The association formally announced its establishment yesterday with a circular telegram and an announcement: (1) The circular telegram reads: “To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the National Government of the Republic of China, all ministries, the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, all bureaus, all provincial and municipal party headquarters, provincial and municipal governments, and all organizations, for your inspection: In accordance with the resolution of the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Conference on the 13th of this month, the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee was organized, and the nomination was sent through the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters for review and approval. Hou Dachun, Wang Wenhua, Wang Zhuping, Lu Jingshi, Li Yongxiang, Chen Peide, Tang Junsheng, Zhou Xuexiang, Wang Xiaolai, Zheng Chengqing, Wang Hanliang, Fang Jiaobo, Ye Huijun, Wang Yansong, Yu Qiaqing, Chen Songyuan, Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Cheng Zhusun, Wang Jian, Chen Xingzhuang, Liu Shimu, Zhang Minghai, Tao Baichuan, Tong Xingbai, Feng Yixian, Chen Yafu, Zhang Huijun, Lin Kecong, Wang Xiaoying, Chen Tingrui, Li Cishan, Yan E’sheng, Zhu Yingpeng, Xi Yushu, Li Wenjie, etc., thirty-seven individuals, were appointed as committee members. The committee was established on [blank space] of this month and immediately held its first committee meeting, electing Yu Qiaqing as chairman of the committee, and Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Hou Dachun, Chen Tingrui, and Lu Jingshi as standing committee members. The committee decided to establish its headquarters in the Tianhou Palace on North Henan Road, and work began immediately. The seal of the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee [seal] is now in use. This special telegram is sent to report for your inspection, and we respectfully request your guidance at any time to facilitate progress. We are deeply grateful and hopeful. The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee kowtows.” (2) The announcement reads: “In accordance with the resolution of the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Conference on the 13th of this month, the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee was organized, and thirty-seven committee members were nominated, reviewed, and approved by the Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters. The committee was established on the 17th of this month, with headquarters located in the Tianhou Palace on North Henan Road in Shanghai. The seal is now in use and work has begun. In addition to reporting via circular telegram, this announcement is made.”

Request for Funds: The association telegraphed the National Government yesterday, requesting an immediate allocation of one million yuan to send personnel to Korea to comfort and rescue overseas compatriots. The original telegram reads: “To the Nanjing National Government, for your inspection: The overseas Chinese in Korea have suffered tragic persecution, causing deep wounds and necessitating urgent relief. Please immediately allocate one million yuan and dispatch a special commissioner to provide comfort and rescue, relieving their distress. We are deeply grateful and earnestly pray. Yu Qiaqing, Chairman, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Tao Baichuan, Hou Dachun, Chen Tingrui, and Lu Jingshi, Standing Committee Members, of the Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee, kowtow.”

Handling of Japanese Goods: The association officially announced its measures for handling Japanese goods yesterday as follows: (1) The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Committee announces the measures for handling Japanese goods in accordance with the resolution of the committee’s first meeting: (A) Orders already placed should be canceled as soon as possible. (B) Orders not yet shipped should be stopped from loading. (C) Goods already in warehouses but not yet paid for should not be taken. (D) Goods already purchased should be registered with the association first and their sale temporarily suspended. Those who violate the above four measures will be severely punished in accordance with the prescribed disciplinary regulations. Apart from the registration rules and disciplinary regulations, which will be announced separately, these measures are hereby announced. It is hoped that all merchants in the city will pay attention and comply. This announcement is of utmost importance. (2) A letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce reads: “To the esteemed members: It has been found that the Japanese, taking advantage of the Wanbaoshan Incident, instigated Koreans to violently expel the Chinese, and overseas Chinese compatriots are now in dire straits. Remaining is not enough to maintain a livelihood, and returning lacks the funds to sustain them. It is insufficient to simply gather donations to provide assistance and meet urgent needs. Therefore, the first committee meeting of this association resolved to send a circular telegram to domestic and international organizations to donate to the relief effort and designated the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Bank, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, the Central Bank, and the four savings societies of the four banks, and the Fuyuan Money Shop as collection agencies. In addition to sending separate letters, a copy of this resolution is enclosed for your information. We hope that you will investigate, assist in collecting and storing the funds, and remit them when a sufficient amount has been collected. This is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and other eight institutions.”

Raising Relief Funds: Regarding fundraising correspondence, the following announcement is made: "Overseas Chinese compatriots in Korea are being persecuted, suffering deaths, displacement, and extreme cruelty. Relief and comfort are urgently needed. The first committee meeting of this association has resolved to begin raising relief funds immediately. We hope that compatriots from all walks of life, patriotic individuals, will enthusiastically provide assistance and generously donate to relieve suffering and save lives. We await your contributions respectfully. Collection agencies: Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Four Savings Societies of the Four Banks, Fuyuan Money Shop. Members of the Economic Management Committee: Qin Runqing, Chen Guangfu, Zhang Gongquan, Xu Jiqing, Qian Xinzhi, Xi Yushu."

Request to Form a Supervisory Committee: The association submitted a document to the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday requesting the formation of a Supervisory Committee: “Regarding the request for the appointment of personnel to form a Supervisory Committee, for your review: The list of committee members for this association was previously nominated by the All-Circles Representatives Conference and submitted to your esteemed association for review and determination. Hou Dachun and two others were designated to be responsible for convening the first meeting, all of which is on record. The conveners convened the first committee meeting on July 17th at the regular meeting room of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. It was resolved to form a Supervisory Committee to ensure the integrity of the organization. The list of committee members is submitted to your esteemed association for appointment to ensure solemnity. This document is prepared for your consideration, requesting your review and instructions to facilitate progress and serve the public interest. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party of the Shanghai Special Municipality.”

Expressions from All Circles: (1) The Minhang Chamber of Commerce of Shanghai County sent a circular telegram: “To all newspaper offices, all chambers of commerce, all trade associations, all professional associations, all organizations, for your inspection: A telegram was recently sent to the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government stating: ‘To the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, for your inspection: The Japanese imperialists, using the Wanbaoshan Incident as an excuse, instigated Koreans to massacre overseas Chinese. This cruelty and barbarity is unprecedented. All those with blood and qi feel pain. We urge you to strongly protest to assert national rights and maintain our nation. The Minhang Chamber of Commerce of Shanghai County, respectfully, [seal]’ We hope that you will unite and rise up to be the government's rearguard. Respectfully transmitted, the Minhang Chamber of Commerce of Shanghai County, respectfully, [seal].” (2) The Shanghai Silk Thread Trade Association held its third executive committee meeting yesterday afternoon. Chairman Zhang Qixiong proposed that since the Wanbaoshan tragedy, all industries have risen up to boycott Japanese goods to support the government. The association should discuss how to respond. It was unanimously resolved that the association would automatically stop ordering Japanese goods. The names of purchased goods and the quantities in stock should be registered with the association within one week. Those who violate the above resolution and selfishly import goods will be severely punished in accordance with the disciplinary regulations prescribed by the Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Association, etc. (3) The Woolen Fabric Trade Association sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday, stating (above omitted). “The association has a patriotic heart to save the nation by destroying homes, starting with economic severance as a tool of passive resistance. This telegram is sent with trepidation and urgency. The Executive Committee of the Shanghai Woolen Fabric Trade Association, respectfully, [sound of whistling]” (4) The Second District Branch of the Citizens' Federation issued a declaration, stating (above omitted). “All our compatriots must unite and resolutely sever economic ties with Japan. At the same time, we urge the government to seriously negotiate with the Japanese government. All members of our association pledge to first boycott Japanese goods as a diplomatic rearguard. We will never give up until the goals of punishing the murderers, compensating the victims, and issuing an apology are achieved. This declaration is hereby made.” (5) The Fudan Alumni Association initiated a general meeting yesterday to address the Korean anti-Chinese incident. Jin Tongyin presided over the meeting. The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting. Chen Binhe and Wu Songgao then gave speeches on the causes of the current Korean anti-Chinese incident and the methods of coping with it in the future. Finally, students were encouraged to unite and rise up as a diplomatic rearguard. Li Quanshi then reported on his participation in the Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid-to-Compatriots Association. Finally, five student representatives and four faculty representatives were elected to jointly form an anti-Japanese association to work hard on everything.

Amidst the Boycott Movement

Japanese Goods Imports Surge Instead

Old and Damaged Stock Sold Out: Since the establishment of the Anti-Japanese Association and the proposal for economic severance with Japan, there have been rumors that the Association would prohibit the import of Japanese goods starting on the 14th. Since the news spread, various places outside Shanghai, deeply concerned that Japanese goods would not be able to enter China, took advantage of the remaining stock to rush to Shanghai to purchase large quantities of Japanese goods for resale elsewhere. Japanese merchants in Shanghai, seeing the large number of buyers, not only raised prices but also sold old stock accumulated in Shanghai warehouses to the Chinese, and required cash payment. Even those with prior transactions were required to pay with ten-day checks. Buyers, only seeking to obtain goods, did not care about quality, resulting in the inferior goods in Shanghai being swept clean. Therefore, Japanese merchants have been happily showing their faces, considering this a blessing in disguise.

Increased Exports on the Yangtze River: Yesterday, of the goods loaded on ships from Shanghai companies bound for the Yangtze River, 60% were Japanese goods, including Japanese sugar, cloth, and kelp. Even the Chinese merchant ships loaded a considerable amount. Over 90,000 bags of Japanese sugar originally stored in Shanghai have now been completely shipped out. In addition, Japanese goods accounted for over 40% of the exports on ships to the northern and southern oceans. The reason for the rush to load is that merchants in various places heard that Shanghai would hold an all-industry anti-Japanese association to automatically boycott Japanese goods on the 27th of this month. They took advantage of the time before the meeting to rush to ship the goods first.

Continuous Arrival of Imported Japanese Goods: Inferior goods transported from Japan by ships such as the Maya Maru and the Rokko Maru have been unloaded in Shanghai in recent days. There are also two batches of goods loaded on the Ikoma Maru, the Amagi Maru, and the Taian Maru that are already on their way and will arrive soon. On the Yangtze River, the Kinkai Yusen Kaisha has dispatched ten ships to rush the goods directly to Jiujiang and Hankou. In addition, Mitsui and Kawasaki have also dispatched ships to transport goods to Shanghai. Despite the proposal to ban Japanese goods starting on the 14th, they are still being transported here in a continuous stream.

Customs Leadership Orders Pilots

To Resume Work Tomorrow Morning

However, Whether the Guild Accepts This Must Be Decided at Tomorrow Morning’s Meeting: The Shanghai Pilots' Guild has been on strike since the afternoon of the 16th, for three and a half days. Not a single foreign ship entering or leaving Shanghai has had an official pilot. The Port Director of the Jianghai Customs, along with the Shanghai Consular Corps and the Joint Association of British and American Chambers of Commerce, convened a meeting yesterday morning at the Jianghai Customs Building on the Bund. It was decided that the Jianghai Customs would reissue pilot licenses and that the Port Director of the Jianghai Customs would send a letter to all members of the Shanghai Pilots' Guild at 3 PM yesterday, ordering them to resume work unconditionally tomorrow morning (Monday). The Shanghai Pilots' Guild, upon receiving the letter from the Jianghai Customs, convened a meeting at 4 PM yesterday to discuss the matter. The situation yesterday is recorded as follows:

Meeting of the Three Organizations: At 10:30 AM yesterday, the Port Director of the Jianghai Customs, Mr. Green, convened a joint meeting in the conference hall on the third floor of the Customs Building with the Shanghai Consular Corps, representatives from the Joint Association of British and American Chambers of Commerce. Present were Mr. Green, Port Director of the Jianghai Customs, Mr. Hellman, Chief Inspector, Mr. Cunningham, US Consul General, Mr. Scottie, British Vice Consul, and representatives from the Joint Association of British and American Chambers of Commerce, including Mr. McTaggart (General Manager of Dodwell & Co.) and Mr. Frantel (Manager of Jardine, Matheson & Co.), totaling seventeen people. The meeting lasted for approximately two hours and adjourned at 12:30 PM. After the meeting, Mr. Green, Port Director of the Jianghai Customs, told a New Life News reporter that the meeting resulted in a decision to first order the Pilots' Guild to unconditionally resume work on Monday and issue pilot licenses at the same time. If members of the guild are unwilling to resume work by the deadline, a second meeting will be convened on Tuesday to discuss further measures.

Meeting of the Pilots: The Pilots' Guild at No. 26 The Bund convened a meeting of all members at the guild yesterday afternoon upon receiving the letter from the Customs. Thirty-eight people were present, chaired by Mr. Philip. The meeting lasted for approximately one hour and adjourned at 5 PM. After the meeting, members and Chairman Philip stated that the meeting only reported the contents of the letter received from the Customs. There was no definite expression on whether to accept the unconditional resumption of work. A meeting will be held again on Monday morning to discuss the matter.

Temporary Pilotage Law: Regarding the entry and exit of foreign ships, the Customs has established a temporary measure, temporarily assigning several anchoring instructors under the Customs to guide the ships. Therefore, there should not be any major difficulties for ships entering and exiting. The rumor of a complete standstill is not accurate.

Ships Entering and Exiting Yesterday: Although the entry and exit of ships have experienced difficulties due to the lack of pilots, the Customs has assigned anchoring instructors to temporarily act as pilots, so the entry and exit of ships is barely normal. The ships that entered yesterday included the 比里敦 at 7:25 AM from Hong Kong and the 威爾福來德 at 4:40 PM from Qinhuangdao. The ships that exited included the 奔奈爾號, 馬牙丸, 達特南號, 錫爾威堡號, 萬考威爾城, 凡彫木得號, 威爾特號, and many others, all bound for foreign waters.

Losses of the Pilots' Guild: The losses of the Pilots' Guild and all its members in recent days have been considerable. It is estimated that the guild's daily expenses and the daily income of its members average a loss of over two thousand taels per day, totaling nearly ten thousand taels.

Retains the New Municipal Committee Member Zhu Yingpeng

Zhang Zhijiang and Niu Yongjian

Yesterday Hosted the Press Corps for Martial Arts

Lectures on the Necessity of Promoting Martial Arts

Zhang Zhijiang, President of the Central National Martial Arts Academy, and Niu Yongjian, Vice President, spare no effort in promoting martial arts. In order to promote the nationwide effort, they hosted the press corps at the Dongya Restaurant yesterday evening. Zhang and Niu gave earnest speeches on the necessity of paying attention to martial arts. Zhang Zhijiang’s speech stated that the Central National Martial Arts Academy has been established for several years, and the number of letters from all over the country requesting martial arts teachers is overwhelming. Therefore, it is necessary to expand the Central National Martial Arts Academy. There are many Chinese who are skilled in martial arts, but those in the past only had skills and no knowledge, so it is planned to first collect these talents, train them, and then gradually promote them to the people of the country. Chinese people have always been called the "sick men of East Asia". If we want to wash away this shame, we can only create martial arts to train our bodies. Only with strong bodies can we have new ideas and achieve great careers. Niu Yongjian’s speech stated that the key to the disparity between the strength of China and Japan is that Japan has a national army, while we do not. Only when the whole country is a military can the whole country be mobilized, and the people of the whole country can be well trained. Military training is secondary. It is not difficult to train soldiers. They can fight in two or three months and be trainers in five or six months. Martial arts is our country's original military science. In the event of melee combat, it can make up for the lack of modern military science. However, its training is not refined in two or three years. The Chinese people should catch up as soon as possible and prepare early. I am not preparing for militarism and aggression, but with this preparation, we can use it or not, we can be fearless, and without this preparation, we cannot use it and can only be slaughtered. Therefore, the Chinese people should wake up and prepare early. Then, Shen Zhuowu and Qu Shaoyi gave reply speeches on behalf of the press corps.

County Police Refresher School

Held Opening Ceremony Yesterday

Since the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau was reorganized, the County Government has earnestly reorganized and prepared to establish a long-term police refresher school in accordance with provincial orders, and entered the school in stages for training. The opening ceremony was held at 10 AM yesterday. The heads of various bureaus, district chiefs, heads of various public security sub-bureaus, officials of the Public Security Section of the County Government, and guests, as well as various long-term police officers, totaling more than 200 people, were present. County Chief Yan presided over the meeting. After the meeting, everyone stood at attention, sang the party song, and paid the highest respect to the party's national flag and the portrait of the Premier. The chairman respectfully read the will and observed silence. Then, the chairman reported (the speech is recorded separately below). Next, Peng Liren, standing committee member of the county party headquarters, Shi She, head of the county education bureau, Ye Dezhen, secretary of the county, Bi Huan, chief of the fourth district, and Zhao Lian, head of the second public security sub-bureau, gave speeches in succession. After the speeches, photos were taken and the meeting was adjourned. The following is County Chief Yan's report:

Today is the opening day of the County Police Refresher School. We should first explain the reason for holding this refresher school. This time, the school is being held on the one hand to comply with the orders of the Ministry, and on the other hand, to address the factual needs of public security in the county. The responsibility of the police is very important, especially at the time when self-government is being promoted. It is not enough to only passively resist bandits and suppress opium and gambling. We must actively help the implementation of governance. During the period of political tutelage, the county is a self-governing unit. However, the county is still too large and complicated, and the relationship with the people is not the most direct and intimate. The organs at the lower level and the people have the most direct and intimate relationship, such as the district office and the various district public security bureaus. The promotion of self-government cannot but rely on these two organs. Therefore, household registration and health are all the responsibilities of the police. However, the actual situation is far from satisfactory. The basic responsibility of the police is to maintain local security. Without local security, there is no way to talk about self-government. However, some of the police officers do not even understand the exercises and how to use guns in terms of skill. As for those who are illiterate, there are still many. Without basic knowledge, all matters of self-government cannot be understood. How can they be responsible for promoting it? In the past, the county could not pay attention to training because the police salary was too difficult. As a result, whether in terms of skill or in terms of academics, the foundation was too shallow and could not be restudied. This time, in accordance with the orders of the Ministry, we prepare to train all the police officers in the county in rotation within one year, with two months as one term. However, the period of two months is too short. It is impossible to learn everything in this short period. These two months of refresher courses are like giving you a key to unlock the door of the school. Everything in the school requires you to explore and examine after you return to work. For example, in academic subjects, there is party ideology and criminal law. How can we teach you anything in just a few hours? The refresher school teaches you an outline, and in the future you can follow this path to study. With such a difficult public economy, the police affairs are very busy. These two months of refresher courses are very valuable. You should pay close attention to the instructions of the officials and do not neglect them in the slightest. You should especially cherish and preserve the handouts you receive. If you do not understand, you can ask the officials and do not waste time. Furthermore, a person's knowledge is certainly important, but morality is especially important. The first thing the police must do is to respect discipline and govern themselves before they can govern others. In the future, you will have to maintain social customs and hygiene. Therefore, your discipline and hygiene must be given special attention. After you return, you will still have to serve. The school will determine the promotion and demotion of your positions based on your performance in the refresher school, and will not make any false assumptions. Furthermore, the heads of the various sub-bureaus are all here today. The refresher course for two months is very short. In the future, you must stipulate methods to increase training at any time and in any place, whether in terms of skill or academics. This is the responsibility of the heads of the various sub-bureaus.

Plans to Establish Three Faculties: Engineering, Commerce, and Law

Fundraising Goal of Three Million Yuan

Gu and Dai Memorial Service Scheduled

Morning of the 25th

The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-American Soldiers' Atrocity Association has scheduled a memorial service for the tragic deaths of Mr. Gu Jingen and Mr. Dai Tingzu, who were killed by American soldiers, to be held at 9:00 AM on the 25th of this month in the auditorium of the Municipal Party Headquarters. The association sent a letter yesterday inviting all circles to attend at that time. The original letter is as follows: To whom it may concern, Mr. Gu Jingen, a carpenter in the Construction Department of the Taichang Company of this port, was tragically shot and killed by American soldier Fuhufusi (transliteration) at No. 15, Gongping Road, Broadway, on the evening of April 22, 1931. Furthermore, Mr. Dai Tingzu, a dock vendor, was tragically pushed into the Huangpu River and drowned by American soldiers Pai Lan'erru (transliteration) and Shi Jilitar (transliteration) in front of Cargo Depot No. 8, Jinliyuan Wharf, Zhaoshang Bureau, in this port at 3:00 PM on May 23 of the same year. The news of these tragedies has deeply pained us all. These men were no less than national heroes who sacrificed themselves for the country due to the illegal privileges of American soldiers who massacred citizens of the great Republic of China like Gu and Dai. Recalling the past and present, our sorrow is immeasurable. In addition to our association leading all circles to actively take action to avenge the nation's humiliation and restore national rights, we have scheduled a memorial service to be held on Saturday, July 25, at 9:00 AM in the auditorium of the Municipal Party Headquarters to commemorate their heroic spirits. In addition to sending letters to all groups to send representatives to participate, we hereby send this letter to inform you and hope that you will send representatives to participate at that time. If you wish to present memorial banners or eulogies, please send them to the Anti-American Soldiers' Atrocity Association within the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union.

Anti-American Soldiers' Atrocity Association

Letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association

Request to Send a Letter to Correct the Letter from the American Consul General

The Shanghai All-Circles Anti-American Soldiers' Atrocity Committee yesterday sent a letter to the Taxpayers' Association requesting them to write again to the American Consul General. The letter states: "We have read the letter from the American Consul General to your association, which vaguely states that the Chinese judge in the case of the shooting of Gu Jingen recognized it as an act of self-defense by the American soldier, and that Dai Tingzu accidentally drowned and the cause of his falling into the water could not be ascertained. However, the American soldiers, in order to comfort the father of the vendor, gave him a pension of 250 yuan to settle the case. As for the case of the stabbing of four people at the Qichang Warehouse in Pudong, they claimed to be unaware of it because it was not reported to the consulate, and that our public announcements in the newspapers were harsh and the wording was false, which must be refuted. After investigation, Gu Jingen, a docile carpenter with bare hands, was shot and killed by an American soldier in an interior room, with the bullet entering from the door, and after examination by Judge Guo of the Special District Local Court, it was confirmed that he was shot and killed by the murderer. He was sued to the competent yamen. How can this be reversed and considered an act of self-defense? This is the first point. Dai Tingzu, upholding righteousness and aiding others, was confronted by an American soldier in the water, who pushed him into the Huangpu River and drowned him out of resentment. According to the original letter from the Consul General, the American soldier had already given a pension to the family of the deceased. If he was not the person who harmed Dai, why would he do this? This is the second point. As for the case of four people being stabbed by American sailors at the Qichang Warehouse in Pudong, there is a file at the Public Security Bureau that can be verified. There is no room for argument. This is the third point. The Consul General is best at resorting to the organs established by the two governments to resolve disputes according to law. We believe that the establishment of this organ is still impossible, which is tantamount to deceiving people with empty talk. In fact, the relatives, such as Gu Jingen's younger brother, have repeatedly complained to the Consul General's office, and our appeals from all walks of life have piled up like mountains, but the American consulate has turned a deaf ear. However, the only reply in the past few months has been this, which is very disappointing. As for our proper announcement of the news about this case, it is out of justice and righteousness. We sincerely hope that the American consulate will automatically seek a satisfactory solution to the above cases with the same spirit of peace and law-abiding, and not deceive people with empty words and suffer harsh criticism. This would be fortunate indeed. Therefore, we specially request your association to write again to the American Consul General to pay attention to correcting the facts to conform to the truth. July 18th."

Problem of Salvaging Sunken Ships

The Shipping Association Proposes Opposition

The Maritime Law stipulates that the responsibility for salvaging sunken ships belongs to the shipowners, which is unanimously opposed by the shipping companies in Shanghai, and they have already submitted a request to the Legislative Yuan for amendment. Now, because the Jianghai Customs intends to deduct the cost of salvaging sunken ships from the insurance compensation of the sunken ships, the shipping companies of this port have specially proposed opposition to the Shipping Association. The resolutions passed by the representatives of each company are as follows: (A) The shipping companies cannot recognize that the Maritime Law stipulates that the removal of sunken ships is the responsibility of the shipowners and are petitioning for amendment. Even in terms of Article 23 of the Maritime Law, it can only be limited to the value of the ship's voyage, movements, and other incidental expenses, which do not include insurance compensation. It is obvious that it is difficult to illegally mix them together. Moreover, the withholding of funds must go through judicial procedures and cannot be illegally disposed of. The Supervisory Office's approval of this move is not in accordance with legal precedents, and the shipping companies cannot recognize it. Insurance companies should reply and deny it. If the insurance company complies, it should be responsible for it and should not resist the shipping companies that should receive insurance compensation in the future. The Hu'an Company will be notified by the association for investigation, and if necessary, a petition will be submitted in accordance with administrative appeals procedures. (B) The shipping companies find it difficult to reluctantly comply with the Maritime Law's stipulation that the responsibility for removing sunken ships should be borne by them. The association will list the reasons in detail and submit them to the National Government Chairman Chiang, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, the Ministry of Communications, and the Ministry of Finance, appealing for amendment.

Municipal Government

To Discuss the Issue of Business Tax Distribution

The Jiangsu Provincial Government recently submitted a request to the Executive Yuan regarding the issue of business tax distribution, proposing to follow the example of the Hubei Province and distribute the total amount of business tax revenue from the two cities of Nanjing and Shanghai, with 70% going to the provincial government and 30% to the municipal government. After consideration by the Executive Yuan, it was considered that this matter must be negotiated with the municipal governments of Nanjing and Shanghai before a decision could be made, and the Executive Yuan immediately issued an order to the municipal governments of Nanjing and Shanghai to investigate. It is learned that the municipal government considers the impact of this issue on the future administration of the municipal government to be extremely significant and is expected to hold an important meeting to discuss it in detail.

Foreign Firms

Purchase Orders Should be Changed to Use Chinese

The Timber Industry Association Advocates

Representatives Have Been Dispatched to Negotiate Sincerely

The Timber Industry Association of this city, in view of the fact that the order forms used by foreign merchants have always been in foreign languages, and the conditions therein are often one-sided, which not only affects the national dignity but also has a great impact on the interests of the industry, decided at the executive committee meeting on the afternoon of the 16th to elect representatives to negotiate with various foreign merchants. In the future, all documents should be translated into both Chinese and English, and in case of any ambiguity, Chinese should prevail to respect national dignity and balance rights and obligations. Wei Shanfu, the manager of Dao'er Foreign Firm (who is a chairman of the association's committee), immediately acknowledged that he would be responsible for contacting the foreign firms for compliance.

There is More Local News Transferred to the Following Page

Page 15

Local News Two

Robbers Rent a Car to Commit Robbery

Renting a Car for Convenience

Car Rental Companies Should Pay Attention

A robbery occurred at Changyun Lane, Xindagulu Road, at 5:30 PM yesterday. The robbers first rented a car from a car rental company, drove to commit the robbery, and then loaded the stolen goods and fled. When they arrived at Lafayede Road in the French Concession, the robbers abandoned the car and fled without a trace. The details are as follows:

Opening the Door to Robbers: Wu Bingrong, a Ningbo native, runs an electrical appliance store in Hangzhou and also manufactures clothing in Shanghai. He lives at No. 417, Lane 2, Changyun Lane, Xindagulu Road, in the Public Concession. At 5:30 PM yesterday, a beggar came to the door to ask for money. The child in the house opened the door and gave him a copper coin to send him away. Unexpectedly, in a flash, a strange man sneaked into the gate and walked into the courtyard, shouting, "Is there a Mr. Li here?" As Wu's family was about to answer, three more men followed in. Two were wearing Chinese clothes and one was wearing a Western suit, all of them young. They said to the people in the room, "Don't panic," and then took out guns. The women knew they had encountered robbers and remained silent. Two robbers then went upstairs and broke into the bedroom, rummaging through boxes and cabinets, and robbed over eighty yuan in cash. Before leaving, they also took several agate ornaments from the table, totaling about one hundred and several tens of yuan, and fled with the loot.

Car as Transportation: The robbers rented a car from the Guomin Car Company below the Caso Novo Dance Hall on Aiduya Road. The number of the car was 12595. There were three people in the car at the time, one wearing a Western suit and two wearing Chinese clothes. After driving for only a few tens of yards, two more people were waiting on the road. The people in the car asked the driver to stop and wait, and one of them jumped into the car. Then, they drove west and north to Changyun Lane near the Jesus Church on Xindagulu Road and stopped. Three people got out first, and the one wearing a Western suit left the car last, putting three yuan on the seat as fare. The driver did not know that the passengers were robbers using the car for transportation.

Abandoning the Car and Fleeing: When the robbers left Changyun Lane, they heard a police siren and became very flustered. One robber did not have time to get into the car and fled first. The remaining robbers got into the car and pretended to be calm, telling the driver to drive west, turn south onto Tongfu Road, and then pass through Sacred Heart Road in the French Concession to Lafayede Road before stopping. The robbers then calmly abandoned the car and fled. After the English and French Concession police stations received the news, they immediately sent detectives to search for the robbers everywhere.

Huang Chu Jiu's Assets

Two Bids Cancelled

Ge Jiren Expels Ma Zhaoji

Creditors Suffer Great Losses

In the case of the bankruptcy of the Shanghai Riyue Bank and the Great World Amusement Savings Department, the French Concession Court yesterday summoned the accountants Pan Zhaobang and Wu Zheng to open the bidding for Huang Chu Jiu's assets and to explain the various disputes that arose during the bidding process. Then, the creditor's representative, lawyer Dong Yu, stated that when the Huang's assets were bid on the other day, the lawyer and Chen Zhigao went to the site to supervise. The bidder, Ge Jiren, illegally expelled the bidder Ma Zhaoji, etc., and the highest bid by Ma Zhaoji was more than 50,000 taels higher. It was obvious that Ge Jiren intended to sell Huang's assets at a low price. Such illegal actions caused great losses to the creditors, and the lawyer was very dissatisfied. The two accountants, Pan and Wu, did not stop this situation when they saw it on the spot. Now, for the benefit of the creditors, the lawyers requested that the court order the accountants to sell at the highest price, or allow the security deposit under Ge Jiren's name to be retained. Furthermore, lawyer Jiang Yiping stated that various disputes arose due to the bidding. The bidding method was very poor. In order to protect the interests of the creditors, the lawyer requested that the bidding method be cancelled to avoid losses to the creditors. At this point, the creditor representatives' lawyers, Bian Jialu, etc., all agreed. In addition, lawyer Yan Luqing stated that he requested the court to order the liquidator to estimate the total assets of the Gongfa Company and compare the shortage to the total debt, and to collect the amount from each shareholder in proportion first. After the lawyers argued for a long time, Judge Gong ruled that the bidding and sale were difficult, and the two bids were cancelled. It was also heard that creditor representative lawyer Yan Luqing was dissatisfied with the court's judgment on the responsibility of directors and shareholders and planned to invite all creditor representatives to hold a meeting at the Zhongshe Western Restaurant today to discuss everything.

Yesterday's Continued Trial

Case of Privately Purchasing Military Supplies

Both Contracts Have Been Investigated

Both Were Typed on the Same Typewriter

Defendant Added the Word "Guarantee"

Beeck Reported the Matter to the National Government

World-renowned military detective Beeck and Leveresque were previously prosecuted by the Concession Court for posing as military advisors to the National Government and ordering 1.8 million yuan of military supplies from the Lefa Foreign Firm opened by Englishman Lefa at No. 2 Guangdong Road, and forging Lefa's seal. The case has been tried twice, and the details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the Criminal Court Judge Xu Jiashi opened the court to continue the trial. The police station was still represented by lawyer Ru Baoyi. First, Judge Xu questioned Leveresque about how many times he had contacted Lefa about military supplies. Leveresque replied in English, which was translated by translator Jiang Baoliang, saying, "I went to Lefa's office on May 15 to ask if there was any evidence to prove that I was introduced to Lefa Foreign Firm by Carlo. I have known Carlo for three years, but there are no documents to prove it." When asked if Carlo said he was introducing him to military supplies and not to Lefa's office, he replied, "He was indeed introducing me to manage the shipping." Judge Xu then asked Carlo about this matter, but Carlo firmly denied it. The defendant's lawyer immediately stood up and asked Beeck if he knew Lefa. Beeck replied, "I only know that Lefa has formed a party and is close to the Soviet Union, but I don't know him." Judge Xu then questioned Leveresque about how many people were present when he signed the contract. He replied, "Zhang Faying, Zhang's adjutant Mr. Li, Lefa, and Carlo. This was on the 10th. On the 9th, Lefa ordered me to send a letter to Zhang Faying on Tang'en Road. Zhang said that he would not sign without two guarantors." When asked if Zhang Faying had stamped both contracts, he replied, "Both were stamped." When asked where the contract he presented came from since one contract had been handed over to Zhang Faying, he replied, "It was taken from Lefa's office." The police station lawyer Ru immediately asked to question Leveresque, and the court allowed it. Lawyer Ru then asked, "Did you go to Lefa's office on June 10?" He replied, "I went around 10:00 AM." When asked how many people went with him, he replied, "Only me." When asked how many people were there, he replied, "Carlo, Lefa, Zhang Faying, and Zhang's secretary arrived successively after a few minutes, and then they signed the contract. After signing, a place was set aside and sent to witness Zhu Ziyao to sign." When asked if he was told that the contract seen on the 9th was different from the contract on the 10th because the one on the 10th had not been changed, he replied, "I can't be sure." When asked if he had seen the contract before they signed it on the 10th, he replied, "The contract on the 10th was placed on the table. I didn't look at it because I had nothing to do with it." When asked if Zhang Faying had seen it, he replied, "He had seen it." When asked if Zhang knew English, he replied, "I don't know." Lawyer Ru then stated to the court that in addition to accusing Beeck and Leveresque of violating Article 161 of the Criminal Law for disrupting order and forging seals, they were now adding a charge of violating Article 204 of the Criminal Law for altering documents because the contract submitted by the police station as evidence did not have the word "guarantee" after the witness, while the contract submitted by the defendant had the word "guarantee" after the witness. This kind of behavior was enough to damage the witness Carlo Zhu Ziyao, so it was specially charged. Now, the police station has invited experts to the court to prove that the word "guarantee" on the contract submitted by the defendant was added later. Then, Li Mo, the Western deputy head of the fingerprint department of the police station, testified that the contracts submitted by both parties were typed on a typewriter at the same time, and the word "guarantee" was added to the defendant's contract later. Then, Beeck testified that the witness Zhu Ziyao had received 200 yuan from Lefa to help Guangdong, and that he was helping Lefa because he was afraid that the National Government would find out and confiscate all his property. Judge Xu then asked about the report to the National Government. He replied, "I knew that Lefa was selling military supplies to Guangdong, so I obtained the contract and reported it to Song Ziwen, the Minister of Finance of the National Government. Minister Song learned about it and asked me to temporarily keep the contract and hand it over to Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs when he came to Shanghai. Tang came to Shanghai a few days later, and I went to Tang's residence at No. 97 Fukaissen Road to see Tang, and Leveresque told me that Zhu Ziyao was initially unwilling to sign as a witness, but signed after receiving 20,000 yuan." Then, Zhu Ziyao was brought to the case and asked about the 20,000 yuan, but Zhu firmly denied it and said that on Saturday, the 13th of last month, at 5:00 or 6:00 PM, two lawyers, Xuekesi and Shizhuoren, came to my house and represented Leveresque to ask me for a commission, saying that Lefa was unwilling to pay the commission and that I, as the guarantor, should be responsible for it. The price they asked for was 9 yuan per gun, and I forgot the total amount. Because I was only a witness and did not bear the responsibility of a guarantor, I replied that I needed to consider it carefully before they left." The court then summoned lawyer Shi to give evidence. Shi said that Zhu was asking for a new factory owner. On the 13th of last month, he was commissioned by Le to ask Zhu for a commission, so he went to Zhu and urged him to pay Lefa. At that time, I said, "You are a guarantor and should be responsible for urging the payment," and said nothing else. Judge Xu then summoned lawyer Xuekesi for questioning. As it was past noon, he decided to postpone the questioning to another date.

Cheng Xun Sneaks Back to Jiangwan

Yesterday He Was Forced to Leave the Country Again

The Jiangwan shaman Cheng Xun was previously ordered by the Social Affairs Bureau and the Public Security Bureau to have the municipal committee members of the Jiangwan district and the five districts and five offices jointly carry out the expulsion order, and this was reported in various newspapers. One Due to Poverty and Illness

One Due to Family Matters

Bian Haicheng: Bian Haicheng, a native of Funing, is 54 years old. He joined the party from the Tongmenghui and is now a member of the twelfth branch of the sixth district in this city. He served as a member of the former Zhabei Municipal Assembly and has run the Tianlingtang Pharmacy on Xinmin Road, Zhabei, for nearly 20 years. He had no choice but to move to the Laodexiutang Nursing Home at No. 72 Kaifeng Road. Because he has a wife, a son, and a daughter, and life is unsustainable, he struggled to ask old friends for loans, but few responded. Mr. Bian was originally suffering from phlegm madness and is in a very poor and sick state. He lacks the interest in life even more. Occasionally, when he is sober, his words contain world-weariness. He suddenly went out at around 11:00 AM on the 17th of this month. His wife immediately followed him when she heard the news, but did not know where he had gone. She has been searching everywhere for two days, and his life and death are unknown. Yesterday, his wife, Bian Liu, led her nine-year-old daughter and cried and inquired along the way. The situation was extremely miserable. It is said that Mr. Bian was wearing a white bamboo cloth short shirt, white striped gauze pants, black socks, and black shoes when he went out. His left knee was injured and broken, and he had a short beard. If anyone knows of his whereabouts, please notify his family, and it would be a great merit.

Chen Yinsheng: Chen Yinsheng, the nephew of Mr. Chen, a staff member of the press who lives at No. 33 Ximenli, Ximen Road, in the French Concession, ran away from home yesterday morning due to a minor family matter. He is 17 years old, from Chaoyang, Guangdong, and speaks the Jiangbei dialect. If any kind person finds him, please send him to No. 33 Ximenli, Ximen Road, French Concession, Shanghai, or notify his family, and they will be rewarded generously and will not break their promise.

Preferential Treatment for Annual Meeting Transportation

The Chinese Engineering Association will hold its 14th Annual Meeting in Nanjing from August 26th to 29th for four days. It has been approved by the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications that members from various ports can travel to the meeting by train or ship in accordance with the preferential treatment rules of previous years. Regulations of the Public Works Department for Removing Shanties

Reply to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association

Zhu Xueli, Cao Xukun, Xu Naikui, Liu Jinzhu, and other representatives of the shanty towns in the Yangshupu area previously protested against the Public Works Department's deadline for demolishing shanties and sent a letter to the Shanghai Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association for assistance. The association immediately forwarded the letter to the Public Works Department. Yesterday, the Public Works Department replied to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, stating: "With reference to the letter of June 29 protesting the demolition of shanties in the Eastern District, the Bureau has considered moving a small number of shanties for the convenience of filling in low-lying areas, but there is no intention to demolish all shanties immediately. The Bureau has considered this issue and decided to register and stipulate that no new shanties may be built in order to prevent the gradual increase of such unauthorized buildings. It is proposed that the number of existing shanties be reduced year by year by mutual agreement. This is a corresponding reply for your information."

Passenger Baggage Inspection Notice

The Commissioner of Customs of the Jianghai Customs has found that passengers arriving in Shanghai by ship do not store their baggage on board in accordance with the regulations, which is in conflict with the regulations of the Customs. The regulations for the inspection of passenger baggage arriving in Shanghai are as follows: (1) (A) When the ship arrives at the Shanghai wharf, all passengers are not allowed to leave the ship until the baggage has been unloaded and transported to the Customs Inspection Warehouse. (B) All passengers disembarking at the Customs wharf must have their baggage arrive at the wharf before the first passenger ferry or at the same time as the passenger. (2) Each piece of baggage must have a label with the owner's signature or the number assigned by the shipping company. (3) Relatives and friends of passengers and receptionists of transport companies are not allowed to board the ship or passenger ferry without the special permission of the Customs. Only the passenger himself and the agent authorized to transport the baggage are allowed to enter the fence of the inspection warehouse when the baggage is unloaded for inspection. Other persons are not allowed to enter. (4) All baggage must be unloaded as soon as the ship has docked. If baggage is found remaining on board after it has been announced that the unloading has been completed, the shipowner and the ship's agent will be punished. Passengers who do not unload their baggage immediately after arriving at the port shall pay ten taels of customs duty as a special fee. The Customs will facilitate the implementation of this inspection.

Repealing the Zhejiang Road Cemetery Contract

The Municipal Council Disagrees

Not far from the Special District Court on North Zhejiang Road and Alabastos Road, there are the Yi Cemetery lands of Tongren Fuyuan and Bao'an Two Halls. A plaque reading "(Bao'an Hall Name)" still remains. Short walls surround it, with desolate graves and overgrown weeds. It is abandoned and useless. Citizens passing by all sigh, unaware of the history within.

The Municipal Council's Contract Negotiation Process

According to records, the land is located in the "Guo Zi Wei" area of the 25th Bao, 2nd Tu, purchased by Fuyuan Hall and others from Ma Jinhai and others during the Xianfeng 9th year, totaling 29 mu, 5 fen, 7 li, and 4 hao. Current measurements show 33 mu, 1 fen, 3 li, and 5 hao. In the Guangxu 19th year, the Municipal Council considered building a road and occupying the land. The hall established a contract stating that no more coffins should be placed on the land, nor should temporary storage of coffins be allowed. The person in charge was to keep the area clean. In the Guangxu 28th year, the Municipal Council again planned to build a Chinese Children's Public School on the land and colluded with some directors to establish a contract to sell the cemetery land. This was met with heated opposition from citizens, almost leading to turmoil. The directors then purchased a plot of land on Kenenghai Road as a replacement and separately established a contract. The original text reads: "The directors of Shanghai Fuyuan Hall and Bao'an Hall, for the sake of preserving the Yi Cemetery land of Fuyuan Hall and Bao'an Hall in the future, now enter into a contract with the Municipal Council. The agreed-upon clauses are listed below: (1) The Municipal Council has agreed to cancel the recently signed contract for the sale of the Yi Cemetery land of Fuyuan Hall and Bao'an Hall. Hereafter, the directors of Fuyuan Hall, Bao'an Hall, etc., shall never sell or lease the Yi Cemetery land to others, nor shall they use the land for other purposes. (2) All the clauses agreed upon in this contract have been published in Western newspapers and included in the minutes of the Municipal Council Western Directors' meetings, and have also been published in local newspapers so that everyone may know the actual situation. It has also been registered for future reference. Furthermore, this contract shall serve as permanent evidence that the Yi Cemetery land of Fuyuan Hall and Bao'an Hall shall not be used for other purposes in the future. (3) The directors of Fuyuan Hall, Bao'an Hall, etc., have prepared two copies of this contract, signed to show good faith, and affixed the seals of the Shanghai Daotai and the British Consul General to indicate that this contract was approved by the local officials before being established. January 5th, 1902, Guangxu 28th year, October 6th, Tongren Fuyuan Hall Director Cao Jishan, et al."

Motive for Repossession and Use: In recent years, the North Zhejiang Road area has become increasingly prosperous, and the estimated value of the land is over one million silver dollars. The Shanghai Charity Organizations Property Management Committee believes that it should be improved for use to increase revenue and develop charitable undertakings. Therefore, the committee's design division planned in detail, submitted a resolution to the meeting, and requested the Bureau to forward it to the government to negotiate the cancellation of the old contract and then lease the property through public bidding, with the remains to be relocated to rural areas.

Reasons for Repealing the Contract: It is found that the Shanghai Charity Organization has an Yi Cemetery land located near the Special District Court on North Zhejiang Road in the Public Concession, totaling 23 mu, 1 fen, 3 li, and 5 hao. It was formerly the property of Tongren Bao'an Hall and Tongren Fuyuan Hall and is now under the management of the organization. The area is surrounded by dense markets and convenient transportation and has become a prosperous commercial area. It is a great pity to leave it unused. According to the organization's directors, the Public Concession Municipal Council planned to establish a Chinese Children's Public School during the Guangxu 28th year of the late Qing Dynasty and bought the entire cemetery land from the directors of the former Tongren Lai'an Hall and Tongren Fuyuan Hall for the purpose of building school buildings. A contract was signed and completed. However, due to opposition from citizens (against the relocation of graves), the directors Cao Jishan and others were instructed to negotiate the cancellation of the contract. The Municipal Council then purchased another piece of land as a school site and took back the cemetery. When the contract was cancelled, the directors of the two halls entered into a contract with the Municipal Council containing three clauses. The first clause stated that the Municipal Council had agreed to cancel the recently signed contract for the sale of the Yi Cemetery land of Fuyuan Hall and Bao'an Hall, and that hereafter, the directors of Fuyuan Hall, Bao'an Hall, etc., should never sell or lease the Yi Cemetery land to others, nor use the land for other purposes, thus preventing any change in its use. We believe that the entire cemetery land is now estimated to be worth over one million taels, and it is unwise to abandon it for profit. Furthermore, the maximum responsibility for the cancellation of the contract is to compensate for the losses of the cancelled party. Since the land has already been purchased and compensated, the Municipal Council has no losses to speak of. The contract not only restricts the sale but also the use of the owner. This kind of arbitrarily restrictive measure is not permissible according to legal principles. Now, if the graves are relocated and houses are rebuilt for rent, the Shanghai Charity Organization will also be able to obtain a large income for charitable undertakings, and the Municipal Council's property tax can also be increased significantly. After discussion, it was resolved that the contract should be negotiated and cancelled, and it was assumed that the future income from the use of the land would be used to support vagrants or reformatory expenses. The matter was then submitted to the Municipal Government for approval. This is because there are many vagrants in the city and the special district, and some minor criminals do not necessarily need to be imprisoned. The lack of reformatories and shelters only leads to them acquiring bad habits in prison that cannot be redeemed. If a reformatory is established, and criminals are given the opportunity for reform after their release, reducing crime will be equivalent to securing society. If the contract can be cancelled and methods can be found to reorganize the area, using the income to run the above-mentioned undertaking, it will be mutually beneficial. After the Social Affairs Bureau reviewed it and forwarded it to the Municipal Government, an order from the Municipal Government was recently received.

The Municipal Council's Opinion: They do not agree to the cancellation of the contract and have proposed that the land be turned into a park or a permanent open space to avoid overcrowding. The residents there are already considered too numerous, and if shops and residences are rebuilt, the number of people will inevitably increase by tens of thousands. Their intention seems to be for the Municipal Council to buy the land for use as a park or green space for citizens to relax, but there are no definite plans yet. It is said that the Social Affairs Bureau has already forwarded the Municipal Government's order to the Shanghai Charity Organization.

Zhuang Chunfu

Accuses Ren Zhennan of Fraud

Lawyer Ren Zhennan was accused by Zhuang Chunfu, a native of Ningbo, in the Lawyers' Association of defrauding him of 5,500 yuan in settlement fees for a lawsuit involving his concubine, Wang Lianxiang, in the French Concession court. The Lawyers' Association requested the local court to investigate and prosecute. Yesterday, Judge Qian Chengjun continued the trial. Zhuang Chunfu testified that he was 47 years old, a native of Ningbo, and involved in the real estate business. Zhuang Li's was his wife, and Zhuang Jihuai was a distant nephew. (Question) Is Zhuang Li's here today? (Answer) Not here. (Question) With whom are you involved in a lawsuit in the French Concession court? (Answer) My concubine, Wang Lianxiang, is suing me for abuse and bigamy. (Question) Which lawyer did you hire? (Answer) First Fei Xizhen, then Ren Zhennan. (Question) How many hearings did Ren Zhennan attend? (Answer) I attended one hearing when Fei Xizhen was my lawyer, and I also attended one hearing when Ren Zhennan was my lawyer, and then I was detained. (Question) Who found Ren? (Answer) Qian Yumin and Gu Gongda. (Question) When did you meet with Ren? (Answer) February 10th. (Question) Where? (Answer) China Hotel. (Question) Who else was there? (Answer) Zhuang Li's, Qian, Gu, etc. (Question) Did Ren come? (Answer) Yes. (Question) What room number? (Answer) 204. (Question) Who booked it? (Answer) Lawyer Ren. (Question) How much money did you pay? (Answer) 200 taels. (Question) What kind of money? (Answer) Public expenses. (Question) Any other money? (Answer) On the 12th, I paid another 500 taels. (Question) What kind of money? (Answer) Handling fee for the opposing lawyer, Zheng Yuxiu. (Question) When did they say that? (Answer) That day. (Question) Where was the money paid? (Answer) China Hotel. (Question) What room number? (Answer) 204. (Question) Any other money? (Answer) 1,000 yuan was paid on February 22nd, and a check for 3,000 yuan and 500 yuan was paid on the 23rd. It was paid at the office, and my wife went with me. They said it was a settlement fee. (Question) Why isn't Qian Yumin here? His lawyer then presented an airmail letter from Qian Yumin, requesting that its contents be read and presented in written form, etc. The judge read it and returned it, saying that although the Lawyers' Association had questioned Qian Yumin, the court should directly question Qian Yumin and ask him to testify. Zhuang could only agree. (Question) Zhuang Jihuai, state your age. (Answer) 43 years old, from Ningbo, engaged in real estate, residing at 22 Hanbi Road. (Question) How do you address Zhuang Chunfu? (Answer) Paternal uncle. (Question) Do you know about your uncle's lawsuit in the French Concession court? (Answer) Yes. (Question) Do you know about hiring Ren Zhennan? (Answer) No. (Question) Do you know Ren? (Answer) I didn't know him before. (Question) How did you go to his office? (Answer) Lawyer Fei Xizhen was introduced by me. Later, I heard my aunt say that the matter could be settled, and she mentioned Lawyer Ren. (Question) Have you been to his office? (Answer) Outside of February 20th. (Question) How many people went? (Answer) I went alone. (Question) How did they come? (Answer) I went to Lawyer Ren's office and introduced myself. Zhuang Chunfu, etc., came soon after. (Question) Why did you go? (Answer) To ask about how to settle the matter. Later, Zhuang Chunfu, etc., gave Lawyer Ren a stack of banknotes, the amount of which I don't know. Two days later, when it was time for the hearing, I went to the China Hotel to ask Lawyer Ren. (Question) What number in the China Hotel? (Answer) I don't remember. (Question) Which floor? (Answer) About the third or fourth floor. (Question) What did you go for? (Answer) To inquire about the settlement situation. (Question) Where was Ren Zhennan's public expense paid? (Answer) At the office. (Question) What about the 500 taels handling fee? (Answer) No. (Question) Do you have any counter-evidence? (Answer) He said the 500 taels handling fee was before the settlement. (Question) Why did you have to pay 500 taels to the opposing lawyer? (Answer) There is no such reason. (Question) What about the 4,500 yuan? (Answer) He said it was a settlement fee. Zhuang Jihuai was an introducer at Fei Xizhen's office and knows a little bit about things. He couldn't just pay me over 4,000 yuan based on my word. If I wanted 10,000, would I also pay 10,000? (Question) How many times have you been to the China Hotel? (Answer) During the New Year, friends opened a room on the sixth floor to play cards. The alleged room 204 can be investigated. The judge said that this would definitely be investigated. (Question) If you didn't take the money, would people accuse you for no reason? And why would Zhuang Jihuai want to speak against you? (Answer) Zhuang Jihuai is his relative, and he was the one who introduced Fei Xizhen. He certainly doesn't sympathize with me. And if the settlement fee was collected, was there a receipt? (Question) No receipt was issued for the settlement fee? (Answer) If there was a settlement fee, both parties should have gathered together to pay it in person. It couldn't be paid in installments so casually. The judge concluded that the witnesses in this case were not all present and that further investigation was needed, and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Fire in Qibao Town, Western Shanghai

Qibao Town in western Shanghai, located on the border of Shangsong and Qing, is a prosperous market town. The streets north and south of Tang Bridge are the most bustling. Since the town was built, the streets have been narrow, and the buildings on both sides have been built over the allowed height. Once a fire breaks out, it is inevitable that it will spread like wildfire. Around 7 PM the day before yesterday, a fire broke out in a certain family, immediately bursting through the roof, with flames that were too bright to approach. Coupled with the urgent north wind, the fire spread even more rapidly. The town has no firefighting equipment, so once the fire started, they were at a loss and could not control it. The fire spread from Tang Bridge to the pawnshop street, burning down over twenty houses, destroying the essence of the entire town, until halfway through.

Coast Patrol Office

Sends Warships to Strictly Investigate Japanese Fishermen Smuggling

Japanese Fishing Vessels Have Disappeared from this Port

Japanese fishing vessels have been encroaching on the coastal waters of China. Customs offices across the country have been ordered to prohibit foreign vessels under 100 tons from entering Chinese ports and to clearly stipulate that Japanese fishing vessels entering China to smuggle goods should pay import duties of 2.20 Japanese yen per 100 catties, equivalent to 4.50 Chinese yuan. More than 60 Japanese hand-operated net fishing vessels, such as "Man Qian Maru," "Ping Yu Maru," and "Zhao Sheng Maru," which were fishing in Shanghai, have gradually stopped coming to Shanghai due to the tariff issue and have now disappeared, instead going to Qingdao. The Shanghai Fisheries Guidance Institute recently dispatched technician Wang Defa to consult with Yan Qiwu, secretary of the Coast Patrol Office of the Naval Department, to discuss measures to crack down on unscrupulous merchants transporting Japanese fishing vessels to Shanghai. As a result, the Coast Patrol Office will send two patrol ships to conduct strict patrols day and night along the coast from the mouth of the Huangpu River to the mouth of the Yangtze River. If Japanese fishing vessels are found docked along the coast, they will be driven away. If unscrupulous merchants are found smuggling Japanese fishing vessels, they will be severely punished according to the law.

Chinese Officials

Carefully Investigate the Whereabouts of the British Teenager

The British Embassy Has Informed the Taopeng Family

After the British teenager Taopeng disappeared from the port on May 31st, the British Consulate General's Office heard rumors that two Chinese military police officers were shot and injured by Westerners near Kunshan on the night of June 1st. They immediately detained a foreigner, suspecting that the detained foreigner might be Taopeng. They sent personnel to visit Kunshan and Suzhou to investigate. The British Embassy also requested the National Government to send personnel to investigate. The Ministry of the Army and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs each sent personnel to Suzhou and found that there were no foreigners detained in the local garrison prison. They also went to Kunshan and found that the local military police had not detained any foreigners. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs then informed the British Embassy of the committee's investigation results and notified them that they had already instructed the civil and military officials of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provinces to carefully investigate Taopeng's whereabouts. According to Western newspapers, the British Consulate General's Office in this port has received the embassy's reply and has informed the teenager's family.

The Concubine Claims it is Her Younger Sister

Three Times Colluding to Release Doves
